<Author>Ghauri75
<Content>Don't waste your money! We went for a Xmas break and choose it for its prime location, when we saw our room we both thought.... its tiny!! i mean how were we both going to get changed and move around in it??? It had no natural light only a tiny window near our feet with the view of a buildings roof!!! There was no tea, coffee or water in the room not a single english channel on the oversized TV. Tiles in the shower were mouldy, No Clock ...basics we expect from a 3 star in europe!!! When asked to move we were told the hotel was full.As for the free tea and pastries at reception....well the tea tasted like TCP (Had to buy tea from down the round every evening, so its not the milk they use in spain as we first thought)and the coffee had been brewing all day so was like tar. The pasties were hard dryed up crossaints which tasted like cardboard.The room cleaning only happens in the morning, so if you want a lie in, your room doesnt get cleaned or get your towels replaced.Staff were friendly but were always trying to sell you something...the tourist bus tickets...which were such a rip up.26 euros for a bus tickets that is always overcrowed, only ever goes in one direction...so if you see a sight and want to go back you have to sit the entire 1hour 20 minutes of the bus ride to get back to the stop you got on. As it was raining couldn't sit upstairs and see the views. The buses only run up to about 6 in the evening at some stations. Metro is so much better.Save your money and book in a hotel you can actually move around in, and know time of the day it is outside.

<Author>skybluefan
<Content>Good hotel, great location This hotel is in a fantastic location - right in the heart of the Bari Gotic. The rooms are very clean, comfortable and well equipped. If you are planning on spending a lot of time in the hotel (you're in Barcelona, why would you??) you might find it a little basic. Because of its location the rooms are relatively small and the facilities a little limited (small bar, terrace, pc for internet access) but If you are there to enjoy all the wonderful things Barcelona has to offer I'd say its and ideal place to stay.

<Author>Debla24
<Content>Loved the H10 ..... I have just returned from a 3 night stay with my 66 year old mother at the H10 Raco Del Pi. I had stayed at the 4 star Olivia Plaza on my previous visit to Barcelona, but this hotel far exceeded my expectations in terms of price, quality and customer service for a 3 star rating. Check in was quick and simple and the welcome glass of cava was a really nice touch. Reception staff helpful in suggesting restaurants, etc. The room was spacious with sufficient wardrobe space. Twin beds with 'ever so soft' pillows and extra pillows and blankets provided. Bathroom standard size with good supply of toiletries and towels changed daily. The free afternoon coffee, tea, water and pastries were great after a day of shopping or sightseeing. Yes, the pastries were probably left overs from breakfast as suggested by another reviewer, but hey they were free and would only have been thrown away! The location was ideal - just a couple minutes off Las Ramblas. This was a last minute booking, that I made after reading other Trip Advisor recommendations - and they were not wrong. My mother and I both agree that we would definitely recommend the H10 to anyone looking for a good value for money hotel in the centre of Barcelona.

<Author>nodata
<Content>Absolutely fantastic! My husband and I spent 6 nights at the H10 Raco Del Pi at the beginning of September. We loved it! When I booked I asked politely for a room with a balcony. Not only did we get a balcony - we got two! Our room had 14 foot ceilings and balconies with double opening doors on two walls. Does it get any better than this? Honestly, it was beyond perfect. It was quite hot the week we were there and we really appreciated the air conditioning too. This was a normally priced room, not an upgrade in any way.Many other people have mentioned the large, clean modern bathrooms, and ours fit that description as well. The location is unbeatable as well. We could walk to see so much - Las Ramblas, the beach area, La Raval, the Cathedral, many of the museums, some great shopping, loads of restaurants, and, of course, some of Gaudi's works. The metro is a few moments walk from the hotel for everything you can't get to by foot.We had nothing to complain about in the noise department. Yes, the street is full of people during the day, but even so, when we closed our doors it was quiet in the room. And at night there is hardly a soul.The staff were super friendly and helpful. We had no problems for them to solve, but they always greeted us with a smile and a friendly word whether we were coming in or going out.This hotel really lives up to its billing. I would heartily recommend it to anyone and everyone.

<Author>shadepalm
<Content>Friendly staff, great location! We relied on the comments of Trip Advisor members and were very happy with our choice for a short stay in Barcelona. This hotel is well located for walking and a short taxi ride from the train station. Good tapas bars close by. Very friendly staff greets you with a glass of Cava. Nice! The room was small but very clean. The bathroom was very nice with everything you need including lots of hot water. We are mature travelers with lots of miles traveled and would stay at this property again. The breakfast, albeit expensive, was delicious. Plenty of protein to keep you going. We found this property to be a very good value in an expensive city. A word of caution: the taxi drivers in Barcelona range from world class diplomats to snarly characters who know very little of the geography of the city and pretend not to understand a word of English. We had both. There is a minimum charge of 10 Euros from the airport for a taxi. One of the most expensive taxi systems we have every experienced, anywhere. The train from the airport to the city and outlying areas works very well.

<Author>croftonMelbourne
<Content>Comfortable and friendly We stayed at H10 Hotel Raco del Pi Barcelona for 3 nights in August 2008. We are a mature couple who like to explore on foot, getting the real flavour of a city, its people and culture so we tend to research the location where we wish to stay thoroughly. We describe ourselves as backpackers at heart who have matured to enjoy reasonably comfortable accommodation. We chose Raco del Pi because it is conveniently located in the old city (Barrio Gotic) with narrow alleys and streets, surrounded by reasonable quality, low cost restaurants and close to Las Ramblas, subway etc and a short walk to the Plaza Catalunya shopping precinct and open top bus routes.The hotel staff were always helpful and enjoyed the welcome class of champagne on arrival. We always request a quiet room and they obliged, with the street noise from mainly foot traffic disappearing by mid evening. The room was reasonably large, bathroom was clean, a fridge in the room and air conditioned. The room was serviced daily and whilst our chosen price range does not provide 5 star sparkle, the hotel was clean and comfortable with a good shower. We will return to Raco del Pi without hesitation.

<Author>aureus30
<Content>Gret location We got the bus from the airport to Place de Catalunya, it was a 5 minute walk to the hotel, just off La Rambla. The receptionist was very friendly, we were offered a free glass of cava. The room and bathroom were very nice. There is free internet access on the ground floor, next to the bar. Breakfast is expensive 10-15 euro so we didn't have it. There is a bakery just across from the hotel (go left exiting the hotel, it's about 15 metres) that sell lovely filled croissants so I'd recommend there. Between about 2pm and 6pm in the hotel, there are croissants and rolls (presumably breakfast leftovers) on the bar along with coffee and you can help yourself for free. All in all it was an excellent hotel, only lacking a swimming pool, but there are plenty of buses to the beach. If going to the beach I would recommend going up to the far end by the Olympic Port (outside hotel Arts), the beach is a lot quieter there.

<Author>987654321abc
<Content>The location was the best thing about the hotel Great location. <Author>scoobydoobie
<Content>Wonderful Location. Didn't like the beds. Hotel H10 Raco del Pi is terrifically located in the heart of the Barri Gotic on a street that is fairly busy during the day but absolutely dead quiet at night. It can be just a tad bit difficult to find the hotel again for the first time once you've made your initial journey out of it, but that's part of the beauty of staying there. The staff are very nice, the rooms are modern and clean, my only complaint with them was that the bed was not very comfortable to me. Were it not for the bed, I'd give the hotel five stars. One other thing, you have to pay an extra 2 euros per day if you want a key to use the safe in the room. Overall, this was a nice hotel in terms of location and qulaity of the room, other than it being just a little small (but perfectly adequate with a clean and updated bathroom too). The price was a bit high, not that the rooms aren't nice, but they definitely milk their location a little. I'd stay there again as a sure bet but I'd be interested for curiosity's sake to try someplace else next time in Barcelona.

<Author>Blundellsands
<Content>Great location This is a good hotel in a great location, ideally situated just off La Rambla and less than 10 mins walk from Placa Catalunya where the airport bus stops! You are met with a welcome glass of Cava on arrival and there are coffee, water and cakes available all day free of charge, which is great after sightseeing! The breakfast was excellent both in choice and quality, there being both hot and cold dishes. The room we had was at the top of the hotel with a small window at floor level, but it was large and well appointed with a spa bath in the bathroom! There are plenty of restaurants nearby, but we found Barcelona generally more impersonal and expensive than other Spanish cities we have visited, and that includes Madrid! However, everything Gaudi is memorable, and if you like football a visit to Camp Nou is a must!

<Author>gingersmum
<Content>Dissappointed! We have just returned after spending 3 nights at this hotel and we were very disappointed!As a result of reading some reviews, I took the trouble to email the hotel to explain that our visit was for a special occassion (our wedding anniversary) and please could we have one of the larger rooms at the front,overlooking the street.They completely ignored my letter and we were given a very small room at the back,with a view of a brick wall! I did go back to reception and they offered me the same room on another floor but with no windows!!(Although we had a window,the curtains were too narrow and there was a big gap down the middle so we were unable to make it dark...at least no one was able to see in due to being overlooked by the brick wall!)Our room was so small that we were unable to move around the bed at the same time ,so had to take it in turns to lie on the bed to enable the other to get ready.The bathroom was ok though except the shower sprayed the floor ,and all our stuff ,until we got used to it!On arrival we were offered the breakfast deal i.e.if you paid up front for all days you could have the first day half price.It was 16 Euros each! Expensive,but we decided that if we ate loads we wouldnt need to bother with lunch.This is what we did ,and it worked well.They also wanted us to pay in cash (for some reason their credit card machine was missing!) we refused as we didnt want to tie up E82 of our cash and guess what...the machine had reappeared the next morning!Very weird!As it is a buffet you can obviously pick and choose but if you are not fussy it was fine.There was : fruit juices,cereals,fresh fruit (lovely selection),cheeses,hams,smoked salmon,rolls,bread,yoghurts,croissants and a good selection of other pastries.Hot food was the same every day: scrambled egg,bacon,fried egg and sausage (the german kind).it was never very hot but was quite tasty.The free drinks and pastries in the foyer that others have mentioned are actually whats left from breakfast and usually ended up being croissants.There was never any hot water left to make tea so we managed with a cup of stewed coffee from an urn.But hey it was free!I have to say that everywhere was very clean and the staff were friendly enough.The position of this hotel is good for walking to lots of places although we felt very uneasy on the Ramblas and tried to avoid it as much as possible.To and from the airport we used the Aerobus which was great and really easy.4.05 Euros each,each way (tried to buy a return ticket but didnt seem possible).It drops you in Pl Catalunya and from there its about 10 min walk.A few other things I should mention: there is no lounge or bar in this hotel and they do not serve any other food apart from the breakfasts.There was free internet access in the foyer and also some newspapers available.Take earplugs as we were woken up at 3am every morning by people clattering down the hard floors and talking loudly!

<Content>Great Location, Great Value I stayed in this hotel for 2 nights recently and was very pleased with our choice. Three of our party of 12 were pickpocketed and there can be an uneasy air around the Ramblas at night. We never let any of our group walk alone at night. That aside, its a fantastic city and is really worth visiting.

<Author>MartHel
<Content>24 - 27 Jan 2008 We have just returned from a 3 night stay at the H10 Raco del Pi.We had a brilliant time in Barcelona and loved this hotel. We took ages to choose a hotel after reading numerous reviews and we were pleased with our choice. The hotel is tucked down a side street very close to Las Ramblas so in a brilliant location. We had complimentary cava on arrival and the complimentary coffee/tea and pastries provided throughout the day were great especially after a busy day out round the city.The staff on reception spoke very good English and were very helpful. We had room 407 on the 4th floor. It is on the back of the hotel so was lovely and quite but it only had two small skylights and a very small low level window (at ankle level!) so felt a bit dark. However it was clean and had everything we needed and to be honest you dont spend much time in the room so we didnt grumble. Looking at the floorplan on the back of our door we shall ask for room 402 next time which was much larger and had a balcony, but it it is on the front of the hotel so imagine it might be a bit noisy at night at busy times of the year. We would definitely recommend this hotel, particularly because of its position.We would also recommend using the aerobus to travel to and from the airport. It went from right outside the terminal to the centre at Placa de Catalyna and cost just 3.90 euros each. It runs every 15 mins even on Sundays and is less than a 10 min walk to the hotel.The hop on hop off Turistic bus is a must. The red tour round the north of the city was more interesting and we used it to get to and from the Nou Camp.For a lovely evening meal we would recommend Attic. A fab restaurant on Las Ramblas. Its above some shops about a third of the way down Las Ramblas. At night you cant miss it as you look up to see a modern and inviting restaurant overlooking the street with a queue of people waiting for tables! It was great to sit at the window watching the entertainers and people going by below whilst enjoying a lovely meal. It cost about 80 euros for a 3 course meal and a good bottle of wine. We loved it so much we went twice but would advise you to book a table or go before 8pm as there was always a queue after 8.30pm because its so popular.One word of warning - be careful about having a drink at the tables in the middle of Las Ramblas. We stopped for a rest and had 2 beers (not large ones) and they presented us with a bill for 15 euros! They charged us 7.50 euros each for a glass of San Miguel!! What a rip off - so ask the cost before you order.We absolutely loved Barcelona and will definitely return and stay at H10 Raco del Pi.

<Author>aapje
<Content>Quirky but attractive, good but expensive It's a little quirky - your experience depends a lot on which room you get; they vary considerably. We started in room 110, which was a dark stifling airless box with a sealed window completely overlooked by the courtyard bar. The a/c was useless and there was no hot water. If this happens to you, ask early the next morning to move to another room [they can arrange this before the following night's guests arrive] rather than ask them to repair the problems, because the latter won't happen.... We were moved to the third floor and a room with a lovely little balcony overlooking the Carrera del Pi - much more what we wanted!The Raco has many plus points, but if you get landed with a poor room, it's not worth the money unless you can change.

<Author>JaLor
<Content>Neat, clean and priced right Good location for access to the Rambla, Cathedral and Gaudy.Hard to find since it is tucked away down one of the little side streets off a courtyard, but it all adds to the atmosphere of Barcelona. Don't count on your GPS since it is hard to pick up a signal among the buildings.The rooms are good size for Europe and more like N.American size. Clean with comfortable bed. Nice roomy clean washrooms with lots of hot water. Clean lobby, halls and stairways. The lift is a bit shakey and slow but works and can actually hold a few people. Don't count on the internet access since the desk staff can't figure out how to connect, although there seems to be access points on each floor. They still have one computer in lobby which is usually relatively easy to get on.Staff are very pleasant and eager to help (even if they can't). Speak English well and can always get there message across. Didn't eat in the hotel although they do have a morning breakfast.The area is very entertaining; lot's of hussle and bussel(particulary on the Saturday--but dead quiet on Sunday -- surprising!) and many places to eat. Just sit on the Rambla and have a nice tall cold beer and watch the activity. Cathedral is a short walk away and Gaudy can be reached on foot but will take about 15-20 mins. Metro nearby but I would recommend a taxi if coming in from the airport for about 20euro. If going to Port Vell another 20e (special fees to port + luggage charges).Sorry, no pictures of hotel since all have me in them struggling to get the internet connection!

<Author>SHJ199
<Content>On a city break ? Stay here. So you're planning a city break to Barcelona ? Never been before? You're reading all of the reviews but can't decide where to stay ? When you don't know the city at all, it's so confusing having to weigh up the various permutations and options. After all, you want to enjoy the trip, not be let down by a bad choice of hotel, right ? I had the same difficulties, but am very glad that I opted for the Raco del Pi.If you want roof-top pools, plush facilities or funky interiors to relax in whilst visiting a great city, this hotel is not for you. However, if you want a clean, comfortable and friendly base for exploring the delights of the city on a long weekend, with little time to waste, Raco del Pi will suit you perfectly.Previous reviewers have not lied. The location is absolutely PERFECT (in the heart of the gothic quarter). The discreet entrance is on a pedestrian only street (though taxis can pick-up / drop off at the door). The Cathedral is only a moment鈥檚 stroll away. In the opposite direction Las Ramblas is no further. Shops and cafes abound. Similarly, the waterfront area, museums and main central tourist sties can all be easily reached on foot from the front door. This truly is a central location.We booked a standard double room just one week before our 3 night trip. The only request I made was for it to be non-smoking. We were greeted by a friendly 鈥淗ola鈥? a glass of Cava and a front facing room of ample size on the first floor, with a balcony view of the street below. The bathroom (with customary toiletries) was large enough for a bidet. Both rooms were spotlessly clean and a room safe allowed us to store valuables. The beds are firm but very comfortable and the air conditioning can be easily controlled by a wall thermostat.The rate was for a room only, but we welcomed not being 鈥渢ied in鈥?to breakfast in the hotel (though it was extensive and a 50% discount was offered for the first morning). English newspapers lay on a table for guests to read. If you prefer, there is a very pleasant coffee shop 10yds up the street serving a wide selection of pastries or a pretty church square 50yds the other way with two cafes. We were happy to mix it up.All of the staff are very friendly and helpful. Complimentary tea, coffee and pastries are available every afternoon and the free Internet is also available for guest use. If you have a late departure, the hotel will gladly store your cases after check-out so you can enjoy the last few hours in the city.We both enjoy staying in more opulent hotels, but on a city break with so much to offer, the amount of time spent in them doesn鈥檛 justify their cost. Not once did we regret booking this hotel.You can waste your time looking at more options if you want to, but at the Raco del Pi you won鈥檛 be wasting any time in Barcelona鈥?

<Author>WalesTraveller
<Content>Good, central Barcelona hotel We recently stayed in this hotel for 2 nights. It is in an excellent location, not far from the Ramblas (and hence the Metro station) as well as the Gothic quarter, the Cathedral etc. There are plenty of bars and restaurants close by. As many others have said, the rooms are fairly small and although not spectacularly decorated, they are adequate and clean. The bathroom was quite a good size though. There is a little atrium courtyard in the middle of the hotel which is nice to relax in and read a book after a busy day in Barcelona. One downside to this hotel is that there is only one (tiny) lift which is incredibly slow and you have to wait a while for it come! Many times we just gave up!The reception staff were very friendly and welcoming, especially with the free glass of cava on arrival! The free tea/ coffee/ croissants etc during the day was also a nice touch, as well as free internet access if you need it. The breakfast was included in the price of our stay and it was pretty decent.Overall we thought this hotel was quite good value for money considering its central location.

<Content>Wonderful experience Just returned from wonderful 4 day break at the Raco del Pi and just cannot find fault with any part of our stay at all. The location of the hotel is second to none - nestled in the very heart of the gothic area, close to shops, las ramblas and catalunya square. The room also had two small balconies, one overlooking the pedestrian street (great for people watching with a glass of cava) and the other overlooking a quiet service alley, it was great to open the doors just to soak up the murmur of the street below, without the noise becoming intrusive. We did not eat breakfast at the hotel, but we did enjoy the complimentary coffee and pastries which were always fresh and a welcoming after a long day (or night) out. The hotel staff were also very friendly, offering advice and personal recommendations. Highly recommend this hotel - book direct for best rooms (appx 鈧?42 for 3 nights) .

<Author>MrandMrsDuck
<Content>Great small hotel in fantastic location Just returned from a four day stay at this great little hotel. The location is perfect right in the heart of the gothic quarter. Our room was small (207) and had no view - but having said that, the room was clean  had everything we needed (except no tea/coffee making facilities - I don't know about anyone else but I need a caffine fix in the morning so poor Nick had to get up and pop out to the coffee shop and bring it back up to the room - no great hardship as it was only 50 paces away). The staff on the front desk were very helpful and always smiling. We would definately stay here again because I think to location is pretty hard to beat - I would ask in advance though for one of the larger rooms and bring my travel kettle (for the early morning brew!!!). A couple of tips for places to see. We loved the Spanish Village (which you can get to from the Blue Route on the tourist bus (very good value and a great way to orientate yourself with the city). We had a lazy afternoon including a leisurely lunch and found it to be a nice restbite from the hustle  bustle of the city centre. Cuitadella park was another quiet spot to while away a couple of hours. A great eating place was Sinatra's which is located just off the Plaza de Reil. It's a minute away from one of the main restaurants right on the square that always has a queue!! Another is down on the marina. It is actually a moored boat but I can't remember the name (but there is only one that's a restuarent too) and they did the best tapas we had all trip. All in all a great little hotel in a fab location in an amazing city. Anyone thinking about visiting - should just go and book it  ENJOY...

<Author>bubble23
<Content>Fantastic location We stayed at the Raco del Pi for 4 wonderful nights and found it to be exactly as people had described - fantastic! The location can't be beaten, right in the heart of everything, with tapas bars, restaurants, sights and local transport links all within a stones throw. The Ramblas is about a 10 minute walk away, with loads of little squares and alfresco bars to quench your thirst along the way! Just as people have said, it is really quiet at night and the hotel's airconditioning is fab. Yes the rooms are small, but to be honest, the cleanliness, location and staff make up for it. We didn't have the breaksfast, as we weren't staying on a BB basis, and it was really expensive (about 15 euros) per person, but there were loads of little places just outside so there was no problem. It did look great though so if you get a deal including breakfast then go for it!The only negative that we found with the location, and it is really minor, is that when the shutters go down, it is quite tricky to navigate your way back through the little winding streets to find the hotel, as all the streets look the same. It took us a few days of trundling around late at night to get our bearings in the dark, which was fun, after a few sangrias, but a little scary if you're alone i would imagine! Also, although the cleanliness of the streets has been mentioned, their methods haven't! As a youngish girl (!) with a penchant for high heals, and a tendancy to get very sore feet late in the evening, I was quite surprised by the ritual spraying of the streets from about 1:30 in the morning onwards. I have normally kicked my heels off by this point, but I learnt my lesson pretty quickly after the 3rd night of slimy and rather yucky feet, to plan ahead and either not wear shoes that will need kicking off, or avoid the sprayers - tricky when they spray the whole of the Ramblas and gothic quarter! Not a complaint in the slightest, but something I wish I had been aware of before going out on the raz!! I would definitely go back to Raco del Pi, and would recommend it to anyone wishing to visit the grogeous Barcelona!  
<Date>Jul 22, 2007

<Author>beekay458
<Content>Well-located boutique hotel The H10 Raco del Pi is well-located in the Gothic Quarter of BCLN. You just walk out of your front door and you are in the thick of stores, tapas bars, and the beauty of BCLN streetlife. (BCLN is one of the cleanest big cities I have ever visited. They obviously spend a lot of money on keeping their city clean.) Despite the busy location, street noise was not a factor.The H10 is a smallish boutique hotel. It is meticulously clean although, as others have mentioned, the rooms are definitely small. We did not have a computer along and but a guest did complain to me about the WIFI signal. There was a free public computer with printer available for guest use. Mineral water and small snacks are available in the bar. There is a beautiful courtyard in the center of the building which we enjoyed using. The beds were hard but comfortable. The AC worked but not to the degree that one of our friends would have liked. The breakfast, although expensive, was very extensive and filling.

<Author>PapaEdwin
<Content>Awesome Little Hotel in the center of everything First of all thanks to all the people that takes their time to write these reviews. It was very helpfull to read what other people has to say about the places they stay. Everything everrybody says about this hotel is true. I was very happy to haved read these reviews here and found out that I made the right choice. The hotel is like a Boutique Hotel, Rooms are spacious, very high cellings, nice closets, good air conditiong units and they are clean. The staff is very friendly and willing to help you with anything. The rooms have balconies so you can go out and watch the crowd pass by. I didnt see any other hotels in the area. The area is mostly pedestrian. If you travel by car you will need a special permit to go thru that street and there is no parking spot there. So you will have to leave your car about 200 meters from the hotel. By 11:00 pm the crowd is gone so you will have no problems with the noise. Women beware of the blower. If you have long hair or like to blow dry your hair, take your own blower. The blowers are 60's type, a case with a long rubber tube and no much heat or air. The rooms have Wi-Fi high speed internet and free use of a computer in the lobby. They provide bottled water on the lobby and also fresh fruits for free. They will receive you with a glass of Cava, a very apreciated gift after ours of long travelling. Breakfast looked great but I didnt had any. There is a Croisanterie in front of the hotel that have all kind of freshly baked pastries and the coffee is the best. When I go back to Barcelona I will stay at the Raco del Pi for shure and hope you do to. I can highly recomend it!

<Author>cmarcel78
<Content>Definitly worth it! Loved this hotel!! In the middle of everything, but also quiet when you want to get some sleep. I shared the room with 2 other people and the space was ample!! We got room 201 and the ceiling was so high and the room spacious. The bathroom was really pretty with the mosaic tiles in deep blue, with double sinks! (There was also a scale, but why depress yourself when you're on vacation). We also had a small balcony that overlooked the walkable street. Didn't take advantage of the breakfast b/c we only stayed 2 nights. But they do offer free coffee and water throughout the day and nuts to snack on.The staff was very helpful and nice. Especially, Albert. He was the best throughout my whole week in Spain.I recommend this place to those who want to be in the middle of action, but also on a quieter street. La Ramblas was 2 turns/ 2 min walk away (where all the loudness and madness is). I don't recommend staying on that street unless you plan not to get any sleep or don't want to relax. Also, the subway was close by as well as walking distance to Playa de Catalunya. This is in the heart of the Gothic quarter and I really did enjoy my stay here.Would either stay here or another H10 hotel when I return to Spain.

<Author>RichardSomerset
<Content>Excellent hotel in great location Just returned from a short break staying at the Raco del Pi in the Barri Gothic, Barcelona. The hotel was excellent - friendly staff, glass of cava on arrival, lovely modern room with balcony overlooking the street of Barri Gothic close to the cathedral. Superb breakfast with variety of fresh fruits, cereals, yoghurt, cheeses, cold meats, bacon  egg. Great location for shops, bars, restaurants and also to La Rambla and Placa Catalunya. Liceu metro is close at hand. Recommend the orange tourist bus (the uofficial one) which takes you on a circuit around all the city's main tourist attractions for 20 euros - you can get on and off as you wish which takes about 2 hours to do the full circuit ( the official red and blue buses cost 19 euros and do a half circuit of the city). You also get discount vouchers to attractions like the Poble Espanyol and La Pedrera. Recommend the restaurants Pla de Garsa, C/Assoanadors (Catalunyan dishes); Les Quinze Nits in Placa Real (it opens at 8.30pm and you need to queue - extremely good value for money (3 course meal with litre of house wine for 4 people 74 euros!), Sinatra restaurant in C/Heures - nouvelle cuisine so order extra potatoes! Must see - the locals dancing the Sardana in front of the Cathedral 6.30pm on Saturdays (and I think at midday on Sundays) and La Pedrera (Casa Mila) - go up onto the roof.

<Author>LaChingona
<Content>Shady Alleys (Don't Trust the Cabs) But a Honeyed Gem in the Tough We booked this hotel last minute, using Tripadvisor's links to venere.com. Thank GOD - although our cab driver didn't know where it was and we had to navigate the deliciously creepy alleys at night looking like complete Yankee tourists (yes, lots of heroin users, no, they didn't bother us), once we got there, it was like heaven. They have delicious free breakfast and free internet! And once we arrived for real, we got a free glass of cava too! H10 Raco Del Pi is a glimmering oasis of calm and modernism in the gritty urban center of Barcelona. It's a stone's throw from the Ramblas and in the middle of the amazing Barri Gotic - full of small alleys and surprising plazas, home to some fanastic shopping. And you MUST try Juicy Jones, a short walk away, for the freshest tasting juices of your life.

<Author>City Seasider
<Content>Excellent. Want to go back soon please! My wife and I stayed between 14 - 17 March, and would certainly stay here again. It has all been said before - excellent staff; very clean room; all the staff speak to you (that doesn't happen everywhere!), and the position could not be better. The complimentary drinks and pastries were very welcome. If you want guaranteed absolute silence day and night though, don't stay here. The hotel is in the middle of a very busy city and, yes, you might be disturbed. We occasionally heard the bells (I am sure they didn't ring all night), and there was a wonderful argument (known as a domestic in the UK) in the alley one evening. I wish my Spanish or Catalan had been better as I am sure I would have learn't some very useful words! It was over as quick as it started, and we both slept very well every night. Stay here, and I dont think you will be disappointed.It was my Wife's birthday whilst we were there, and we had not told the hotel. When we returned on birthday evening there was some chocolates and a very nice hand-written note of congratulation waiting for her in our room from the hotel - a very nice touch that was appreciated. They could only have got the date from her passport copied on arrival - well spotted!We got breakfast out every day, usually for about 7 - 8 Euros each. The bar in the shopping precinct (out of hotel door, turn right, turn right into covered shopping area and walk through) was good. We had excellent lunches (3 courses + drink) for 10 Euros each at Mamacafe (c/del Dr Joaquim Dou) and Anima (c/dels Angels), both in the El Raval area. The El Raval area is on the opposite side to Las Ramblas to the hotel and is well worth a visit in its own right - especially if you want to get away from the tourists.The Bus Turistic (two routes from Placa de Catalunia) at 23 Euros each for two days was good value. Be aware though that not every form of tourist transport runs every day all year round. We were disappointed to find that Tramvia Blau and the associated Funicular Tibidabo only ran at weekends when we were there.And finally. The impression from guide books, etc., is that Barcelona is rife with petty crime. I didn't see anything untoward. I live in a cosmopolitan seaside city and I didn't feel any less safe walking around Barcelona than I do in my own home central area.  
<Date>Mar 22, 2007

<Author>keentoseetuscany
<Content>Excellent hotel in superb location We stayed two nights at this hotel in early February. The location is superb - a minute's walk from La Rambla and about 5-10 mins from the Aerobus stop. The staff were very friendly and we were offered a glass of (very delicious!) cava on arrival. The room was modern and spotless. The bathroom had two washhand basins and a huge array of toiletries including a shaving kit and combs! From reading previous reviews we decided to skip breakfast in the hotel as it was too expensive, however we were offered breakfast on the first morning at a special 50% rate. That was worth it as there is a good selection to choose from. This hotel is situated in the old part of the city and is surrounded by lots of interesting little shops and cafes. If any girls reading this are into jewellery making (as I am) there is an excellent bead shop right beside the hotel. There are several more in the vicinity but some of them are trade only and in some you have to buy a set minimum number of beads. On a practical note the Aerobus is the cheapest way to get from the airport, and very straightforward. Also, as with all cities, stopping for a coffee or snack on La Rambla will be much more expensive than heading off the main street. The food market just off La Rambla is worth going to even if you are just looking! It also has lots of little tapas establishments (counters/stalls) which are packed with locals.

<Author>JAMMY2007
<Content>Just another average hotel. We arrived @10pm and were offered a glass of cava which was a nice start. The receptionist then led us to the room which smelt badly of smoke. I had put in the booking notes we wanted a non-smoking room. We were given a different room which was fine but there were ash trays present so we assumed it was still a smoking room but it was fresh and clean so we took it. During the night it was apparent the air con did not work and the room was stuffy and warm, when I opened the window noise from the alley below was annoying so we closed it again. <Content>We were very disappointed in the Raco Del Pi Having booked and confirmed the Raco Del Pi months in advance we were appalled to find that they had given our room to someone else - although at first they said it was 'a flood in the room' - as we arrived at 6pm, tired from our flight. They then asked us to wheel our suitcases a few blocks to another hotel (The Duc del la Victoria), and requested we come back the next day after 12pm (check-out time). We came back and were given a tiny room at the front of the hotel on the second floor which was incredibly noisy as the street is a pedestrian thoroughfare. We requested a quieter room and were moved to the rear first floor to be woken at 6am after an uncomfortable sleep by the sound of crashing pots and pans - we were above the kitchen!We decided then to go back to the Duc de la Victoria which for the same price had much larger rooms, a really comfortable bed with a proper sprung matress, and a big beautiful bathroom. We also had a big terrace balcony overlooking the bari gotic. The difference in quality of these two hotels was amazing, and i don't understand how the Raco Del Pi is rated 4 star. The rooms are old and tired and small, and the beds thin old traditional unsprung matresses - hopeless for dodgy backs.

<Author>Dritan
<Content>Good hotel at a reasonable price Just returned from a four night stay at this hotel.We paid about 拢70 a night and i thought that was pretty reasonable. Our room was just above the reception and had two patio door/windows. We did get a little lost in the warren of streets on our way to the hotel so give yourself a bit of time to get orientated. It's definitely preferable to stay in the Quarter rather than on Las Ramblas.We were offered the cava on arrival and I had arranged for a bottle of cava to be in our room as it was my husband's birthday during our stay. This was easily arranged via email and the response to the request was very quick. We took the half price breakfast on the first day but didn't bother for the other days as it was too expensive at 14 euros. If they lowered the price to around 10 euros they may get more punters.The room and bathroom were clean and tidy. I quite liked the little radio on the wall - good if you are getting ready for a night out.The minibar was well stocked and not too expensive.For dinner I would really recommend Les Quinze Nits in the nearby Placa Real. We dined here twice and were really impressed. Not used to seeing queues to get into a restaurant and a very large restaurant at that! We had the veal and lamb - really yummy. We also dined at the Taxidermista next door and were frankly underwhelmed. On the safety front, I would advise everyone to invest in a long strapped bag which you can wear across the body. I didn't see any pickpocketing or bag snatching during our visit but couldn't believe that tourists were walking around with their bag slung casually over one shoulder or wearing mini back packs!Overall, a nice little hotel, in a good location.

<Author>rosiekwacker
<Content>fab hotel and city but be careful... Booked this hotel on the basis of reviews on Trip Advisor so felt I had to have my say!! Took my mum to Barcelona for 3 nights to celebrate her 70th birthday so was looking for a central hotel - not too expensive. This hotel is very centrally located - ideal for shopping and exploring the Ramblas. The rooms are clean (if a little too warm and as we were on the first floor over looking the terrace we couldn't open our window) and ours was a nice size with a large bathroom. Majority of the staff were nice and helpful although we were not offered a glass of cava when we arrived - even though it was on the reception desk and I didn't have the guts to ask for it!! Only fault I found with this hotel was the noise level - be warned - bring ear plugs. Regardless of where your room is within the building you will have some noise - because it is located in a pedestrianised shopping district you won't have much traffice noise but you will hear the local church bells, shoppers and late night partiers and also within the hotel, the rooms and corridors are tiled which means that foots steps etc. are quite loud. Also, some rooms are located right next to the lift and stair well which can also be noisy. Aside from that I would highly recommend this hotel - price and comfort could not be beaten and the choice of breakfast in the morning was huge (this was included in our package). Only major downside of our weekend was the fact that my purse was stolen from my handbag - I still have no idea how they got it but when I returned to the hotel after dinner on our last night it was gone. Luckily I had only the bare essentials in it but still - it was a shock to find it gone. I'd like to pride myself on being savvy when it comes to this kind of thing but they are utter professionals - so make use of the safe in your room (only 2 Euro a night) and ensure you use a back pack that is zipped up and has two straps - and preferably keep it to your front. Stay to well lit areas at night and be smart. Barcelona is a fabulous place and I would return again tommorrow but I'd be wiser next time when it comes to personal security.  
<Date>Jan 23, 2007

<Author>Pinchy
<Content>Nice little hotel Having stayed here last week for 3 nights, I have to agree with the other reviews, we didn't bother with a taxi and just got the aerobus from the airport, (3 euros 75) which dropped us off at Plaza Catalunya, and the hotel was about 5 minutes or so away. Again, agree with the checking in, we were offered a glass of cava which was really nice. The free tea, coffee etc are available after 1pm, and run all night., there are only about 3 tables to sit at, so could be a squash if a few people wanted to sit there. We had the breakfast there, which was fine at 50% discount at 7 euros each. We went to Mikos on Las Ramblas the other mornings, and you could get an 'american breakfast' with with coffee for 6 euros 20, but we tried the traditional type,(same price) bread with tomato rubbed on it with serrano ham and cheese, with fresh orange and coffee.I agree about the church bells, it was quite warm when we were there, and I asked at reception about the air con, as there didn't appear to be any, but it is typical Spain, they can't understand why we want to be cold in the winter! We ended up opening the window, so could hear the bells, which didn't bother us too much during the night, but you could really hear them about 8am or 9am.Our bath was very small, I'm 5'2 and I couldn't lie down in it! Nevertheless, everything was nice and clean and in good repair.Again, agree Taller de Tapas was quite expensive, it was good quality, but quite small portions. We ordered clams and beans, which cost nearly 7 euros, and we counted 6 small clams! Good service and good wine though.Excellent location!

<Author>baltorich
<Content>Good hotel, great location, bad beds You can't get a better location right in a pedestrian zone in the heart of Barcelona. The room was quite spacious and the bath, featuring a jacuzzi tub, was huge. We had a room with a balcony overlooking the busy shopping street but the doors did a good job of blocking out most of the noise (if you're noise sensitive though, you don't want a room facing the street). I would've given it 4 stars but the beds are atrocious. I asked for a double bed for two but got the old-school european separate twins that were made separately and pushed together. Even worse were the mattresses which were really very uncomfortable. I can sleep on almost anything but still woke up every morning in pain because the thin mattress was like a rock.The people at reception were very friendly, and it was nice that they regularly provided drinks, snacks and internet usage. Take their security warnings seriously. At 2 in the morning on the second night were were woken up by loud screams from the street where a man walking alone had been mugged and pushed to the ground - literally right in front of the hotel. It's not that the hotel is in a bad area (just the opposite really), but that muggers know that tourists wandering the streets at that hour are easy prey.We took advantage of the first morning 50% off breakfast which was good, but it's definitely not worth the regular 15 euro they charge if it's not included in your room.The only reason I wouldn't stay here again is the beds. They just don't give you the comfort you need after playing tourist all day and night.

<Author>angel84
<Content>Great Hotel, Great Location, Great Holiday! I stayed at Raco from the 20th to 24th November with my sister and mum so age range 22 to 57.First things first, the hotel was great, good location, clean and well presented. Upon arrival, staff were helpful and accomodating - we were given our free glass of Cava and shown around the hotel ammenities, free internet access was great for me and free pastries, coffee and tea served during the day. The hotel did have some downfalls, my sister was given a box room with a skylight for the same price as the double I shared with my mum - which was booked as a twin. The smaller room had a constant dripping noise which no engineer seemed to be able to sort out but in all honesty, these factors did little to discourage my overall impression of the place. The rooms were clean and well stocked with shampoo's, bath gels, shower caps etc which were replenished every day. We didn't venture into the restaurant so I have no review of there other than 30 odd euros seemed expensive for a breakfast when there are a plethora of fantastic pastry shops within easy walking distance. At night, it can be somewhat scary going through small streets but for our four nights there we didn't encounter any problems. To anyone travelling to this hotel, I would strongly suggest putting all your valuables in the safe at only 2 euros per night(plus tax) and take as little out as need be. Despite warnings everywhere about pick pockets, I had my purse stolen as I was jumping on the metro. Be very aware that these people are professinals.Barcelona on the whole was a fantastic place, I was strongly suggest taking the 2 day pass on the bus turistic however, once you get the hang of the bus and metro system, it's really not hard to navigate your way to the sights. The Sagrada Familia is an absolute must! If you are brave enough there are some great places to be found off the beaten track - Hotel Senetor has a fantastic spa open to the public - 3 hours of relaxation, floating in pools with oranges in and a whole host of crazy but fantastic experiences - and at only 15 euros, it is well worth it! In terms of food, Barcelona is not as far as I could tell a vegetarian friendly city. I often found it hard to find something I fancied but experimentation opened my eyes to a world of things I never would have tried. There is a great Veggie restaurant called Organic which is well worth a visit. And Sinatra's round the corner from Placa Real does fab Tapas if you want to try something new.This city is a great place to visit but do invest in a good tourist guide. As a supplement and if you are a bit daring - buy LeCools guide to Barcelona which has some great non-touristy suggestions.Hope this helps anyone contemplating a trip to Barcelona - DO IT!  
<Date>Dec 2, 2006

<Author>martyap
<Content>Great City! Great Location! Just returned from three nights in the Raco del Pi. A short walk to Las Ramblas and as said before a location that cannot be beat. Was in room 204 with a small balcony overlooking Carrer del Pi. Only noise at night was the garbage collection. The area is really quiet after the shops close. At night it is best to stick to the main streets and aviod the dark/quiet ones. Room was clean and functional and the staff was great. Beds were hard but did not prevent us from sleeping after touring all day. Water, pastries and coffee available daily right outside the small breakfast room.We did have breakfast the first night at the 1/2 price rate of 7e...not worth the regular 14e rate...plenty of places to grab breakfast. Right next door is an inside shopping gallery with some cute shops including a very small family owned food counter which opens at 9:00am. Breakfast for two was about 7e. Great fresh squeezed zumo de narranja.We tried Taller de Tapas close to the hotel and was not impressed. Prices were high and food was so-so. If you want tapas go to one of the many small tavernas. Tapas are about 1,60e each and you select right off the counter. They count the toothpicks after and charge you accordingly. Great with beer or cava. Also, go to Placa Real about a ten minute walk. Many great restaurants including Les Quintz Nitz. Join the line about 8:00 pm for the 8:30 seating. VERY reasonable...great variety and super food. Four of us had three courses and wine for 80e. And do not miss grabbing some fruit, a bocadilla or pastries at La Boqueria Market also a ten minute walk right on Las Ramblas. We used the Tourist bus and it was a great way to see the entire city if the weather is good and you can sit on top. We lucked out and it was 68-72 with no rain every day. Taxi cost about 30e to the airport as they do charge a luggage surcharge which seems to have no set rate. Many taxis cannot find the hotel. Heading up Las Ramblas.... turn right after you pass La Boqueria...then the second right on Carrer del Pi.Our friends stayed at the MonteCarlo right on Las Ramblas for three times the price. Room was certainly much nicer but we were glad we picked the Raco del Pi. Will return on our next visit to Barcelona.  
<Date>Nov 11, 2006

<Author>JayPDee
<Content>Okay, but does not live up to the hype The location - absolutely excellent. You couldn't wish for better. Easy walking distance to La Rambla and the underground.The rest was, well, average. We arrived on Friday 29/09 at 7.30pm and were greeted by a full compliment of departing guests hogging reception... waiting for their taxi to the airport. The reception is very small. Eventually the receptionist turned up and copied our passports before advising us we would be staying in room 107. No cava offered...Overlooking a narrow, deserted side-street the room was quite small but very crisp and clean. The bathroom was also small and neat and exhibited the fresh flower and wide range of toiletries as descirbed in previous guest reports. We were lucky enough to have a full height 'patio'-style door that opened onto a very small balcony. The air conditioning worked perfectly despite the daytime temperature averaging 28 degrees, for early October...The breakfast was superb, with every conceivable taste catered for. Although it was charged at 鈧?4 (per person) for the first 2 mornings it was only 鈧? for the 3rd morning, this averages at 拢7.50 (鈧?1.50/$13.50) per day for as much as you can possibly eat and drink, excellent value.The free internet was present but nearly always fully occupied from early in the morning 'til late at night. The free coffee, water and pastries were very pleasant after a long days' trekking but only made up for the lack of such facilities in the guest rooms.Overall a very pleasant stay. For the location and facilities in the great city of Barcelona the H10 Raco del Pi offers a discrete but average experience. Just don't expect 4-star quality for a 3-star price.

<Author>Madre_di_Dios
<Content>Can this be the same hotel everyone else here stayed at? After reading other glowing reviews here about the H10 Raco del Pi in Barcelona, my friend and I booked a double room there more than 6 months in advance of our trip, confident it would be a great place to stay. Our flight arrived in Barcelona very early local time, so when I confirmed our reservation in writing a week in advance of our arrival, I requested early check-in. Nope! They couldn't be bothered to arrange this, not even with a week's advance notice. The hotel did not let us check in a second before 2:00 p.m. Exhausted and unbathed, up for more than 24 hours straight, we had to wander around Barcelona in a sleep-deprived stupor before many places were even open. You can't tell me they couldn't have compromised and had a clean room for us by NOON, with a week's notice, at the very least. Our room was a colossal disappointment. We had room 101, which must be very different from the guest rooms described by other reviewers. It was a dim and depressing 9' x 9' not counting the bathroom. There were no luggage racks, only two tiny sock drawers, and no place to conveniently stow luggage out of our ways, even on the floor. The two beds I'd requested were twin beds with about 2 of space between. If the tile floor was ever swept or mopped the whole time we were there, I'd be surprised, because my socks turned black walking on that floor. The air conditioning and air circulation was beyond abysmal; the air reeked of stale smoke and never, ever changed. Even overnight, even cranked, the air conditioning never quite cut it. Window was locked shut. The front desk staff seemed polite, professional and made earnest attempts to accommodate us, but the housekeeping staff was puzzling at best. Although there were two people in the room, the housekeeping staff only provided towels for one. When we finally got them to start providing enough towels for two, we still couldn't get them to give us an extra washcloth. We left a note with a tip of 3 Euro (we tipped every day about this amount) asking for por favor, uno mas toallita. We returned about 2:00 that afternoon to find both the tip and the note GONE, but our room still not made up. A few minutes later, a housekeeper came by with two more towels, not washcloths. Our Spanish was not so awful that we couldn't hear her cackling to the other housekeepers outside the door about the weirdos in 101 who wanted all the extra towels. From then on, we did not leave tips! Although the tile in the bathroom was lovely, the loose-fitting shower door inevitably allowed a lake of water to leak onto the floor during every shower, and a sole towel hook meant that one of us always had to hang her towel in the closet. The room was also poorly insulated against sound, and late-night partiers lurching around and yelling to one another through the stairwells easily woke us. Our conclusion is that this is a 2-star hotel that charges and masquerades as a 3-star hotel. Although the Barri Gotic is a fascinating neighborhood and very walkable, if you're looking for comfort and cleanliness, I'd recommend going elsewhere.

<Content>Excellent Hotel ! Pros:Location is excellent in middle of gothic quarter, tons of restaurants, shops, plazas, within walking distance of everything. The staff was superb - super friendly. I didn't have a converter for my cell phone charger - they had one for me to borrow so I could charge my phone. It was pouring rain one day - they had umbrellas for the guests to borrow. Free internet access in lobby so you can check your email. Our room had a balcony overlooking the street and was a beautiful view, the bathroom had slate tiled floors, 2 sinks, and a jetted bathtub with shower, fresh flower. You should request a quiet room with a view for these types of things, the hotel usually complies and there is no extra fee for these nicer rooms. The rooms furniture and accents are also new and updated. Feels like the hotel just opened a few months ago.Cons:The hotel is in an area that is not serviced by cars, but alhtough we couldn't take a taxi into the hotel, the hotel was able to arrange a taxi from the hotel door to get to the airport.For 134 EUROS this is an excellent choice.

<Author>Griff_Yorks
<Content>Fabulous Location! We stayed at the Hotel Raco Del Pi on 18th August until the 22nd August. The hotel is really easy to find, we got the airport bus which runs every 15 mins and costs 3.75 Euros, the service terminates at Place De Catalunya and the hotel is just a good 5 mins walk from there.We were greeted by really friendly staff at the hotel reception and offered a nice cold glass of Cava, which was most welcome after the journey! The rooms have a contemporary, modern feel to them, the only slight criticism i would have is some more coathangers in the wardrobe and a chest of drawers would have been handy.The Hotel is just off Las Ramblas in the Barri Gotic, which is a wonderful maze of medieval streets/alleys, it is well situated for all the major attractions, the Metro system and buses are easily accessible.If i visit Barcelona again i would definitely book into this hotel without a second thought.Donna and Adrian, Barnsley, South Yorkshire, England

<Author>minnie_cooper
<Content>A wonderful little hotel I booked this hotel as part of a surprise 60th birthday trip to Barcelona for my Dad, also taking my mother, my partner and 15 month old baby son. I booked on the high recommendations from this website, and the location and price - and I am so glad that I did. My parents absolutely loved it, saying that it was one of the best hotels that they had stayed in (and they're very well travelled!).Our room was a little dark, facing the inside of the courtyard -but it was also quite spacious, which we needed with the supplied babies cot in the room. And my parents room, next door but one, had a beautiful balcony looking out to the street below.Even though the hotel is thoroughly modernised, it hasn't lost the historic character of the original building, with very high beamed ceilings in the rooms and the original stone staircase.The breakfast is well worth getting, with a huge range of delicious food to choose from. An added bonus for us was that the staff were SO lovely to my son, and every morning took him off to meet everyone in the kitchen, which gave me and my partner a welcome break to eat our breakfast in peace.The location is unrivalled in one of the prettiest quiet little streets in the Gothic Quarter, and a 2 minute walk from the amazing food market.All in all, a wonderful stay, at a lovely hotel small enough to retain the personal touch.

<Author>AJOK
<Content>Expensive, Hot, Conjested We stayed at the H10 Raco Del Pi 5-12 July 2006. It was our first visit to Barcelona, and we chose to go to this hotel on previous recommendations posted here. We agreed that the rooms were rather small although the air conditioning was good as it was baking hot outside. The hotel was ok, although a bit expensive, but considering the location was very central, but quite hard to find as all surrounding streets were pedestrians only. La Rambla is only minutes away from the hotel. Breakfast was an extra 拢14 euros per person per day, plus 2 euros per day if you wanted to use the room safe. Free tea  coffee at the small bar, but no tea/coffee making facilities in the rooms, which was disappointing. For those considering taking/hiring a car to get to Barcelona, forget it totally, there are no parking places anywhere. We left our car in a public car park the first night, which cost 23 euros. We then tried to find alternative parking the next day, and found a parking place 8 kilometres from our hotel in the Val De Hebron area, and had to use the subway to get back to the hotel. We left the car there for 3 days, then used the public car park for the rest of the stay. The hotel does have an arrangement for parking around the Cathedral we found out too late, but it's almost 22 euros per night. It's also a nightmare driving in Barcelona, it's always totally conjested, night  day, and you can't even stop to look at a map. Weather was very hot  humid, around 93 degrees most days. Subways are air conditioned and regular, if you can stand the 100 degrees on the platform waiting for the train. All in all it's a nice, clean small hotel, rather expensive tho. Note :- The police will stop you and warn you to be vigilant if they see you're wallet in your back pocket, as there are pick pockets. Also watch out for young women with babies. They gather round you in crowds begging, and looking for something to steal. Prices... as usual the busiest, like La Rambla will set you back 17 euros for 2 drinks (Bacardi/Pint of beer), go a bit further out and prices come down to around 12 euros. After we'd seen the Nucamp Stadium, we used the car to travel to Tarragonna, and Calella  Loret de Mar, very pleasant. Verdict.. nice city, but too hot  humid  conjested to see much of it.

<Author>dandb
<Content>Good Location, Excellent Staff We chose this hotel based on previous reviews and location. We were not disappointed with the location, we loved this area best in Barcelona. The hotel staff were superb, we were welcomed on arrival with a glass of cava, as written about in other reviews, the staff were friendly and helpful throughout our stay. The hotel was modern in decoration and we loved the corridor glass walls view through the to the courtyard below.Our room was on the the 3rd floor, it was beautifully clean. Although not large, the room size was adequate with basic furnishings, the bed was surprisingly comfortable despite being very firm. The only downsides to the room we had were (a) The view out of our room window wasn't great at all (b) It was a smoking room and smelt badly of smoke on our arrival. Unfortunately, our travel agents hadn't passed on our request for non-smoking, and they were none available. However, the duty reception staff arranged to have the room freshened, which immediately cleared the problem for us and finally (c) Our room was close to the lift, which did disturb me late at night.However, we still thought the hotel was very good despite the above. We found the breakfast provided an excellent choice to set you up for the day and the tea/coffee/pastries that you could help yourself to in the bar during the day, a really nice touch along with the free internet facility.If we ever returned to Barcelona, I would choose to stay at this hotel again - but with a request for different room.

<Author>frombaritomiami
<Content>Excellent position, great price/quality ratio I stayed with my wife at Raco del Pi over the last week of May 2006 and it was overall a very good experience. I can repeat all other things that other reviewers have already stressed, but I will concentrate on a few inside tips for this specific hotel.HOW TO GET THERE: Remember oyu are in the Gothic quarter, the taxi will not be able to drop you off in front of the hotel during regular hours, since it is a pedestrian zone, but your walk will be short. On the way back, if you are leaving early in the morning, the cab will definitely pick you up at the door. Just remember the time of the day makes a huge difference between nobody in the streets and hundreds of people walking with you...ROOMS/LOCATION: Location, excellent in the middle of the Gothic quarter. If you have a room with balcony (Rooms 01-04 on each floor) you will have more noise but a larger room. If you stay, like I did, in rooms (08-09) it will be in a smaller room but super quiet (only minor problem in room 309 was that the maid storage room was near our room and when she would come in the morning you could hear her pull the cart and her stuff out of the room).CLEANLINESS/MODERN: Rarely have I seen such a cleaner hotel, and since it is new, all areas exude modern clean taste without looking cold.BREAKFAST: Although lovers of continental breakfast will find everything under the sun in the small restaurant room in the morning, you can have a very large breakfast in the croissanterie right in front of the hotel for a quarter of the price. Only trick (already mentioned): first day is half off, so have breakfast there the first morning until you find a good spot for the following days. The best is the free food left at the bar 24 hours a day for the guests, not so much for the pastries, which are just the leftover from breakfast and get stale by the evening, but for the free water that is a nice gesture since you will be walking a lot in the city and a nice glass of water upon arriving to the hotel before you go to your room is great.INTERNET: It all depends on the other hotel guests: there were days in which nobody would be there, ther were days when one person would be sitting there for hours at a time. Moreover, it is only one computer open to anybody but also to everybody's view, so forget privacy...LOBBY: they do ask you to leave the keys at the desk when you leave (?) they must have had bad experiences, but they are very nice and helpful. Yes, there is free cava (champagne-like wine) but after the first couple of days you want to go and drink it in the bars and restaurants, not in the hotel lobby... Also, remember, the safe is not included in the price, and it is 2 euros a day.OVERALL: To recommend for the best location in a relative quiet area and the clean modern look, great service.  
<Date>May 30, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Beautifully clean and beautifully located Just returned from a 4 night stay in Barcelona at the Raco del Pi. Would highly recommend this boutique hotel to anyone looking for a short stay in the city. It is superbly located - cannot think of a better location, certainly for a first visit to the city. Situated in the narrow lanes by the Ramblas, it is perfect for hopping on to the sight seeing buses - a real must - or strolling out to the shops, and, in the evening, soaking in the historic atmosphere of the squares, the street artists and the open air restaurants. The rooms are compact, but extremely well appointed. The whole hotel is absolutely spotless. The staff are courteous and very helpful. The breakfast is excellent. The internet facilities are free. The atmosphere and presentation of the place exudes polished, simple quality. And, by the way, the room air-conditioning was not only efficient, but unobtrusive - a rarity in my experience.

<Author>CheltenhamFlyer
<Content>Excellent small hotel We booked direct with the hotel in January 2006 via their website for a trip in May 2006. Booking was simple and straightforward. The price actually charged was exactly the price quoted in the email booking confirmation; note however that the price quoted is ex-VAT (7%) although to be fair this is clearly stated. The receptionist also went through the prices very carefully in arrival to make sure we were clear. The only slight niggle was an extra charge for a room safe (2 eruos per night) which was not mentioned anywhere.The hotel is very quiet which for the centre of the Barri Gotic is quite unexpected. However, our room opened on to the central open courtyard rather than the street - outside rooms may be noisier (but you don't go to central Barcelona for peace and solitude do you?) The hotel appears to have been recently refurbished and is a good mixtrue of of the old and modern in terms of architectecure. Brilliant location just down from the Plaza Catalunya and close to the cathedral. It is in the pedestrianised zone so taxi access may be a bit limited - we walked from the Plaza Catalunya where the Airport Bus deposited us (about 10 minutes) and no traffic to worry about.Staff were very friendly and helpful and spoke reasonable English (much better than our Spanish). Our room was an adequate size for two and was spotlessly clean. Internet access is free. There were no tea-making facilties in the room (although there were some self-heating drinks but there was an additional charge for these. However, there is a little bar with self-service tea and coffee (and croissants, rolls and cakes) at no extra charge, and these could be taken up to cool sitting area in a pleasant courtyard on the first floor. I guess this would be nice and cool in summer.Breakfast was excellent and well worth 14 euros extra each (50% discount on the first morning) - huge choice of fruits, cold meats, cheeses, crudites, cereals, cooked bacon and egg etc.The age-range of the clients was wide, a couple of children aged about 10 through to retired couples, and were mostly English, Dutch and American, so far as I could judge

<Author>Rosemary07
<Content>Thoroughly recommend this hotel Stayed for 5 nights at the H10 Raco del Pi, 27 April - 2 May. Previously asked for 'a quiet room on the 2nd or 3rd floor' and got one - room 207 at the back of the hotel. Size OK by European city standards. Spotlessly clean, good bathroom facilities. Room safe, 2 euros a day. No view - overlooked a wall - but not overlooked by anyone. Air conditioning worked fine, at night we could close the window and there was no noise at all. Really quiet for the centre of a major city. If you want a better view, the rooms at the front overlooked the Carrer del Pi, lovely pedestrian street with lots of little shops. These would have had a more attractive outlook but you would have got quite a lot of 'people noise'. Depends what you want, we wanted quiet and got it. Probably best to specify the room location when you book. Other reviewers have mentioned hearing people walking on the hard floors - I have to say we heard virtually no noise of this type. Just one thing - the bed (double) was very hard. We got used to it after the first night.As for the rest of the hotel - friendly efficient welcome including glass of cava. Excellent breakfast - discount rate of 7 euros for first day, thereafter 14 euros. We didn't have breakfast there every day. Coffee/croissants available in the bar area at all hours after breakfast, also apples. Computer in bar area for free internet access. Locked luggage room.Location - we found it very convenient. Ramblas/Liceu metro about 2 minutes walk. Plaza de Catalunya (aerobus to airport) about 5 minutes walk. Gothic quarter was lovely by day, not so attractive at night when shop fronts are covered by metal grilles with graffiti. It felt safe at all times if you stuck to the wider streets, though we weren't out late at night. Took the usual precautions but no problems with pickpockets etc. at any time, didn't see anyone else having problems either. Taller de Tapas just round the corner was a good place to eat. Also liked Trobador in C/ Ferran at the Plaza St Jaume end.We bought the Barcelona Card, ideal for a stay of 5 days, free transport (used the metro) and discount on all admissions. Buy it in advance online, it's cheaper, and pick it up from the tourist office at the airport or the Plaza de Catalunya. For a shorter stay (say 2 days) Bus Turistic would be better. Highlights for us were the Casa Batllo, Sagrada Familia  Palau de la Musica Catalunya. Also had time for a train trip to Montserrat which was lovely, especially if you are prepared to escape the crowds round the monastery and head for the footpaths.

<Content>Perfectly Convenient We stayed here the last week of March and had a great time mainly due to its location and convenience to all centrally located activities. We had a quite room facing the central open atrium not one facing the pedestrian areas...we heard it could be loud at times especially w/ a 2-1/2 year old. If you decide you want a similar quite room request one on the 2nd or 3rd floors. The window level of these floors would be well above the atrium floor and would allow you to leave the window open w/o any concerns. They also have quite rooms facing the back of the hotel which also could be a benefit. The hotel could use some carpet or other sound dampening materials because you will hear people walking on the hard floors at all hours.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>exceptional in many ways we've booked this hotel because of the phantastic location, the reviews we found here, and the price. At 99 euro. Breakfast was not included and was fairly expensive, so we didn't book it. So, when we checked in, they offered Breakfast for half price (7euro per person) - which was really worth it. It included everything we needed, excellent coffee or tea, cereals, bread, fresh fruit, plus eggs and bacon - some of the best i've ever had - and more.The hotel is very clean, we had a room on second floor (#104), which featured two windows and a little balcony to the pedestrian area. the furniture is modern, nice, warm, the ceiling with its thick wooden beams is very high (5 meters?) and astonishingly we couldn't find any spiderwebs as we would've expected :-)there is free internet access on a single computer (a mac, if i remember correctly).the location is just perfect for Barcelona. It's a one minute stroll to the cathedral, or two minutes to the Opera House, which is right there on the Ramblas. Almost directly in front of the hotel is the Church Maria del Pi, where concerts are given (no, they didn't keep us awake at night), and there's a few bars and one of the best tapas-restaurants of the city right at the corner (the one which looks worst from the outside, right where small, dark alleys start. Avoid the touristy looking ones with lots of beer commercials). Walking from the Bus Station (Estacio Nord) to the Hotel took us 20 Minutes, but you can also take the sub and cut this time in half (at least).The Hotel is situated in a pedestrian area, which gets cleaned late at night, maybe also early in the morning. they use motorized vehicles for that, but we didn't have any problems with noise. So, between 11pm and 8am we slept like happy babies.I've read reviews which stated, it's a dangerous area, and a sexshop nearby and so on. Yes, there is a shop called Sexy Shop four or five doors down the road, but to me it didn't look anything more dangereous or suspicious as your average McDonalds-hangout (actually, i cant remember having seen anybody near that shop at all). Barcelona in itself is a difficult city when it comes to street crime. You absolutely have to watch your purse. There are pickpockets everywhere and organized gangs using small children to get what they need. But this is a problem for Barcelona in itself, not for a specific hotel in this extremely beautiful city. So, my conclusion: i've been to Barcelona several times before, stayed in Hotels which were three or four times as expensive, and with the exception of the Arts (which is absolutely breathtaking) none was better than this one. I'd come back here, for sure.  
<Date>Mar 9, 2006

<Author>emmalm
<Content>Great Location The best thing going for the Hotel Raco del Pi is the location. Its perfect for getting to the metro or wandering around the Barri Gotic (Gothic Quarter), there are a couple of pretty squares just around the corner.The hotel is one step up from a travelodge type place, the staff are very helpful and friendly and you are offered a glass of free cava to get you in the holiday mood on arrival. The rooms are not a bad size and are clean. We were a little disappointed as we only had a small slit of a window and two roof top portholes, which meant we didn't have a view (Room 403). As we didn't have a big window to open it got incredibly hot and stuffy in there at night. All in all although it was a great location, I might be tempted to try another hotel in a similar area.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Glad we booked this hotel My wife and I stayed at the Raco DEl Pi from the 1st February 06 for 5 nights. Booked through Expedia (make sure your breakfast is included in price) all our arrangements went smoothly except the taxi driver we used from the bus station had to drop us in La Ramblas as he said he was not allowed in the area around the hotel. This meant dragging our cases 250m through the narrow streets in the late evening. Taxis are allowed in to the area and we booked them through reception on our departure. Could not fault the hotel staff or great breakfast. Room was ok if a little basic. Our room was at the front overlooking the pedestrianised street. Noise was not a problem for me but my wife said there was some noise at night. Area was great for shops and dining out. Nearest tube was in La Ramblas about 200m away. Do buy a Barcelona Card for travel around Barcelona. We bought ours on the internet and then collected it from the TIC in Cataluna Square, 250m from the hotel. One word of warning. Watch out for pickpockets. My wife was targetted at the north bus station after arriving from Girona airport. Luckily she realised what was going on and only lost a pair of glasses.
